        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618549230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7497319887320697541">Fascinating how much of our understanding of what it means to be a <i>good person</i> in Western society stems from concepts deeply incorporated into Buddhism beliefs. <i>The Dhammapada</i> is a collection of aphorisms illustrating the Buddhist moral system. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556206554i/27413114.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>These aphorisms are considered Buddha's own teachings and they deal with endurance, self-control and perfect joy. Despite having been worded hundreds of years ago, most of them are extremely contemporary. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"What we are today comes from our thought of ye</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText7497319887320697541" style="display:none">Fascinating how much of our understanding of what it means to be a <i>good person</i> in Western society stems from concepts deeply incorporated into Buddhism beliefs. <i>The Dhammapada</i> is a collection of aphorisms illustrating the Buddhist moral system. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556206554i/27413114.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These aphorisms are considered Buddha's own teachings and they deal with endurance, self-control and perfect joy. Despite having been worded hundreds of years ago, most of them are extremely contemporary. <br><br><b>
  <i>"What we are today comes from our thought of yesterday, and our present thoughts build our life of tomorrow: our life is the creation of our mind."</i>
</b><br><br>In that regard, we are what we think and our thinking should be positive: forgive others, be strong in your morals and surround yourself with good people. Most thoughts are expressed in a spiritual and philosophical way where it remains open to interpretation how to live your life according to them, but even if you aren't out to practice Buddhism, it's a nice way to familiarize yourself with the key themes of that belief system. <br><br>In 2015 Penguin introduced the Little Black Classics series to celebrate Penguin's 80th birthday. Including little stories from "around the world and across many centuries" as the publisher describes, I have been intrigued to read those for a long time, before finally having started. I hope to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/27203016?shelf=little-black-classics" rel="nofollow noopener">sooner or later read and review all of them</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7497319887320697541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2616335698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616335698" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48922229-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477061923p2/48922229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616335698?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/48922229-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141398815" href="/book/show/24874370-the-dhammapada">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616335698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14853214044528187675">I feel bad reviewing this because I feel like I am being asked to review a religion which is wrong. This is a review of the book only. However the book is essentially the teachings of Buddhism in a nutshell. It’s not exactly surprising stuff - be nice and kind and not a selfish, greedy, evil person. It seems obvious right? But maybe we do need to be reminded sometimes to be a good person.<br/><br/>So what to say about it? … It’s a very long, very repetitive poem teaching the Buddhist way of life and a per</span>
  <span id="freeText14853214044528187675" style="display:none">I feel bad reviewing this because I feel like I am being asked to review a religion which is wrong. This is a review of the book only. However the book is essentially the teachings of Buddhism in a nutshell. It’s not exactly surprising stuff - be nice and kind and not a selfish, greedy, evil person. It seems obvious right? But maybe we do need to be reminded sometimes to be a good person.<br /><br />So what to say about it? … It’s a very long, very repetitive poem teaching the Buddhist way of life and a persons aims in life within Buddhism, it’s a guide. It isn’t something you would read in one sitting and even as poem it is only half there for me, the repetition takes some of the enjoyment out of it - why use a single sentence to explain your meaning when you can write that same sentence 5 times in slightly different ways - I suppose the idea is to drum it into you! It is also quite lecturey, but it is a lesson so it would be wouldn’t it. <br /><br />However having said all that if you take it slowly and think about what you are reading it does work - in small doses. To take any of its meaning in you need to take your time and mull it over. It was quite meditative. I liked to read it on the tube - it helped me feel a little zen when I wanted to kill someone for barging in front of me, my fellow commuters will have to watch themselves now I don’t have the calming power of this book in my hand!<br /><br />So overall not bad, take your time and it might be worth reading but don’t expect anything radical within these pages - just a gentle reminder to be nice and humble. I would suggest that if you are interested in learning more about Buddhism there are other more practical books out there which are more interesting and more helpful. <br /><br />I’m giving this a 4*/5, it was nice in its own way.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14853214044528187675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Joseph Knecht" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63656163-joseph-knecht"><img alt="Joseph Knecht" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496005573p2/63656163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2680477386?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph Knecht" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph Knecht" href="/user/show/63656163-joseph-knecht">Joseph Knecht</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2680477386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12620706641345880467">Small pieces of timeless wisdom. Here are my favourite...<br/><br/>-Long is the night to him who is awake; long is a mile to him who is tired; long is life to the foolish who do not know the true law.<br/><br/>-If a traveller does not meet with one who is his better, or his equal, let him firmly keep to his solitary journey; there is no companionship with a fool.<br/><br/>-If one man conquer in battle a thousand times thousand men, and if another conquer himself, he is the greatest of conquerors.<br/><br/>-Come, look at this glitterin</span>
  <span id="freeText12620706641345880467" style="display:none">Small pieces of timeless wisdom. Here are my favourite...<br /><br />-Long is the night to him who is awake; long is a mile to him who is tired; long is life to the foolish who do not know the true law.<br /><br />-If a traveller does not meet with one who is his better, or his equal, let him firmly keep to his solitary journey; there is no companionship with a fool.<br /><br />-If one man conquer in battle a thousand times thousand men, and if another conquer himself, he is the greatest of conquerors.<br /><br />-Come, look at this glittering world, like unto a royal chariot; the foolish are immersed in it, but the wise do not touch it.<br /><br />-Not to blame, not to strike, to live restrained under the law, to be moderate in eating, to sleep and sit alone, and to dwell on the highest thoughts,—this is the teaching of the Awakened.<br /><br />-He who possesses virtue and intelligence, who is just, speaks the truth, and does what is his own business, him the world will hold dear.<br /><br />-He who, by causing pain to others, wishes to obtain pleasure for himself, he, entangled in the bonds of hatred, will never be free from hatred.<br /></span>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xBjLh6o3jdVOSj9QlA68/d4LDuI0vMo9aQG5a1ESPOAEsBXtd4Q/1VEJ2ZvgCPgbWRpNdqKJeEAWEtv21KLdRw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OzbDB4LJ7Z1W9QcpLDyYc5S3/nxUffgaAzesOCYdhBL7nh1tX3pfnUm24eJYOtyVE6a96MJISmd8JM6lo61ltQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Presented in the for<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10836559822991491206\" style=\"display:none\">One of the great classics of Mahayana Buddhism,  The Way of the Bodhisattva  ( Bodhicharyavatara) is a guide to cultivating the mind of enlightenment, and to generating the qualities of love, compassion, generosity, and patience. Presented in the form of a personal meditation in verse, it outlines the path of the bodhisattvas--those beings who renounce the peace of an individual salvation and vow to work for the deliverance of all beings, and to attain enlightenment for their sake. The text is beloved by Buddhists of all traditions.\n\nOriginally written in India in Sanskrit, the text first appeared in Tibetan translation in the eighth century. The fact that it has been expounded, studied, and practiced in Tibet in an unbroken tradition lends the Tibetan version of the Bodhicharyavatara a particular authority. The present version has therefore been translated from the Tibetan, following a commentary by the Nyingma master Kunzang Pelden, renowned for its thoroughness, clarity, and accessibility.<\/span>\n The classic Sutras (thought-threads), at least 4,000 years old, cover the yogic teachings on ethics, meditation, and physical postures, and provide directions for dealing with situations in daily life. The Sutras are presented here in the purest form, with the original Sanskrit and with translation, transliteration, and commentary by Sri Swami Satchidananda, one of the most respected and revered contemporary Yoga masters. In this classic context, Sri Swamiji offers practical advice based on his own experience for mastering the mind and achieving physical, mental and emotional harmony. <\/span>\n  <a
